href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Cnut the Great</b><sup id="cite_ref-unnecessarycitation_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unnecessarycitation-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">Old English</a>&#58; <i lang="ang" title="Old English language text">Cnut se Micela</i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Norse language">Old Norse</a>: <i lang="non">Kn\xc3\xbatr inn r\xc3\xadki</i><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;995</span><sup id="cite_ref-ArchontologyCanute_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArchontologyCanute-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 12 November 1035), also known as <b>Canute</b>, whose father was <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Forkbeard" title="Sweyn Forkbeard">Sweyn Forkbeard</a> (which gave him the <a href="/wiki/Patronym" class="mw-redirect" title="Patronym">patronym</a> <i lang="ang" title="Old English language text">Sweynsson</i>, Old Norse: <i lang="non">Sveinsson</i>)\xe2\x80\x94was King of <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>; together often referred to as the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Empire" title="North Sea Empire">North Sea Empire</a>. Yet after the deaths of his heirs within a decade of his own, and the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest of England</a> in 1066, this legacy was lost. He is popularly invoked in the context of the legend of <i><a href="/wiki/King_Canute_and_the_tide" title="King Canute and the tide">King Canute and the tide</a></i>, which usually misrepresents him as a deluded monarch believing he has supernatural powers, contrary to the original legend which portrays a wise king who rebuked his courtiers for their fawning behaviour.\n</p><p>As a Danish prince, Cnut won the throne of England in 1016 in the wake of <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age#Northwestern_Europe" title="Viking Age">centuries of Viking activity in northwestern Europe</a>. His latter accession to the Danish throne in 1018 brought the crowns of England and Denmark together. Cnut sought to keep this power-base by uniting Danes and English under cultural bonds of wealth and custom, as well as through sheer brutality. After a decade of conflict with opponents in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>, Cnut claimed the crown of Norway in <a href="/wiki/Trondheim" title="Trondheim">Trondheim</a> in 1028. The Swedish city <a href="/wiki/Sigtuna" title="Sigtuna">Sigtuna</a> was held by Cnut (he had coins struck there that called him king, but there is no narrative record of his occupation).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dominion of England lent the <a href="/wiki/Danes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Danes (Germanic tribe)">Danes</a> an important link to the maritime zone between the islands of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, where Cnut, like his father before him, had a strong interest and wielded much influence among the <a href="/wiki/Norse%E2%80%93Gaels" title="Norse\xe2\x80\x93Gaels">Norse\xe2\x80\x93Gaels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Cnut\'s possession of England\'s <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">dioceses</a> and the continental Diocese of Denmark\xe2\x80\x94with a claim laid upon it by the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Bremen" title="Archbishopric of Bremen">Archdiocese of Hamburg-Bremen</a>\xe2\x80\x94was a source of great prestige and leverage within the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church#Middle_Ages" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> and among the magnates of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a> (gaining notable concessions such as one on the price of the <a href="/wiki/Pallium" title="Pallium">pallium</a> of his bishops, though they still had to travel to obtain the pallium, as well as on the tolls his people had to pay on the way to <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>). After his 1026 victory against Norway and Sweden, and on his way back from Rome where he attended the coronation of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, Cnut, in a letter written for the benefit of his subjects, deemed himself "King of all England and Denmark and the Norwegians and of some of the Swedes".<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The Anglo-Saxon kings used the title "king of the English". Cnut was <i lang="ang" title="Old English language text">ealles Engla landes cyning</i>\xe2\x80\x94"king of all England".  Medieval historian <a href="/wiki/Norman_Cantor" title="Norman Cantor">Norman Cantor</a> called him "the most effective king in Anglo-Saxon history".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div Norway and Sweden</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Influence_in_the_western_sea-ways"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Influence in the western sea-ways</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Relations_with_the_Church"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Relations with the Church</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Death_and_succession"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Death and succession</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Bones_at_Winchester"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Bones at Winchester</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Marriages_and_children"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Marriages and children</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Family_tree"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Family tree</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Cnut&#39;s_skalds"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Cnut\'s <i>skalds</i></span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_and_kingship">Birth and kingship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Birth and kingship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Cnut was a son of the Danish prince <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Forkbeard" title="Sweyn Forkbeard">Sweyn Forkbeard</a>, who was the son and heir to King Harald Bluetooth and thus came from a line of Scandinavian rulers central to the unification of Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Neither the place nor the date of his birth are known. <a href="/wiki/Harthacnut_I_of_Denmark" title="Harthacnut I of Denmark">Harthacnut I of Denmark</a> was the semi-legendary founder of the Danish royal house at the beginning of the 10th century, and his son, <a href="/wiki/Gorm_the_Old" title="Gorm the Old">Gorm the Old</a>, became the first in the official line (the \'Old\' in his name indicates this). <a href="/wiki/Harald_Bluetooth" title="Harald Bluetooth">Harald Bluetooth</a>, Gorm\'s son and Cnut\'s grandfather, was the Danish king at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Scandinavia#Denmark" title="Christianization of Scandinavia">Christianization of Denmark</a>; he became the first Scandinavian king to accept Christianity. \n</p><p><span id="Mother"></span>\nThe <i><a href="/wiki/Thietmar_of_Merseburg#Thietmar&#39;s_Chronicle" title="Thietmar of Merseburg">Chronicon</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Thietmar_of_Merseburg" title="Thietmar of Merseburg">Thietmar of Merseburg</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Encomium_Emmae" class="mw-redirect" title="Encomium Emmae">Encomium Emmae</a></i> report Cnut\'s mother as having been a daughter of <a href="/wiki/Mieszko_I_of_Poland" title="Mieszko I of Poland">Mieszko I of Poland</a>.\n<a href="/wiki/Old_Norse_literature" title="Old Norse literature">Norse</a> sources of the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, most prominently <i><a href="/wiki/Heimskringla" title="Heimskringla">Heimskringla</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Snorri_Sturluson" title="Snorri Sturluson">Snorri Sturluson</a>, also give a Polish princess as Cnut\'s mother, whom they call <a href="/wiki/Gunhild_of_Wenden" title="Gunhild of Wenden">Gunhild</a> and a daughter of <i><a href="/wiki/Burislav" title="Burislav">Burislav</a></i>, the king of <i><a href="/wiki/Wends" title="Wends">Vindland</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\nSince in the Norse <a href="/wiki/Saga" title="Saga">sagas</a> the <i>king of Vindland</i> is always <i>Burislav</i>, this is reconcilable with the assumption that her father was Mieszko (not his son <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_I_Chrobry" class="mw-redirect" title="Boles\xc5\x82aw I Chrobry">Boles\xc5\x82aw</a>). Adam of Bremen in <i><a href="/wiki/Gesta_Hammaburgensis_ecclesiae_pontificum" title="Gesta Hammaburgensis ecclesiae pontificum">Gesta Hammaburgensis ecclesiae pontificum</a></i> is unique in equating Cnut\'s mother (for whom he also produces no name) with the former queen of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Sweden">Sweden</a>, wife of <a href="/wiki/Eric_the_Victorious" title="Eric the Victorious">Eric the Victorious</a> and by this marriage mother of <a href="/wiki/Olof_Sk%C3%B6tkonung" title="Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung">Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\nTo complicate the matter, <i>Heimskringla</i> and other sagas also have Sweyn marrying Eric\'s widow, but she is distinctly another person in these texts, named <i><a href="/wiki/Sigrid_the_Haughty" title="Sigrid the Haughty">Sigrid the Haughty</a></i>, whom Sweyn only marries after <i>Gunhild</i>, the Slavic princess who bore Cnut, has died.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\nDifferent theories regarding the number and ancestry of Sweyn\'s wives (or wife) have been advanced (see <a href="/wiki/Sigrid_the_Haughty" title="Sigrid the Haughty">Sigrid the Haughty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gunhild_of_Wenden" title="Gunhild of Wenden">Gunhild</a>). But since Adam is the only source to equate the identity of Cnut\'s and Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung\'s mother, this is often seen as an error on Adam\'s part, and it is often assumed that Sweyn had two wives, the first being Cnut\'s mother, and the second being the former Queen of Sweden. Cnut\'s brother <a href="/wiki/Harald_II_of_Denmark" title="Harald II of Denmark">Harald</a> was the first-born and <a href="/wiki/Crown_prince" title="Crown prince">crown prince</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_(YORYM_2000_646)_obverse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_%28YORYM_2000_646%29_obverse.jpg/220px-Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_%28YORYM_2000_646%29_obverse.jpg" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_%28YORYM_2000_646%29_obverse.jpg/330px-Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_%28YORYM_2000_646%29_obverse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_%28YORYM_2000_646%29_obverse.jpg/440px-Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_%28YORYM_2000_646%29_obverse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2309" data-file-height="2280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Silver_penny_of_Cnut_the_Great_(YORYM_2000_646)_obverse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Silver penny of Cnut the Great</div></div></div>\n<p>Some hint of Cnut\'s childhood can be found in the <i><a href="/wiki/Flateyjarb%C3%B3k" title="Flateyjarb\xc3\xb3k">Flateyjarb\xc3\xb3k</a></i>, a 13th-century source that says he was taught his soldiery by the chieftain <a href="/wiki/Thorkell_the_Tall" title="Thorkell the Tall">Thorkell the Tall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> brother to <a href="/wiki/Sigvaldi_Strut-Haraldsson" title="Sigvaldi Strut-Haraldsson">Sigurd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jarl_(title)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jarl (title)">Jarl</a> of mythical <a href="/wiki/Jomsborg" title="Jomsborg">Jomsborg</a>, and the legendary <a href="/wiki/Jomvikings" class="mw-redirect" title="Jomvikings">Joms</a>, at their <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> stronghold on the island of <a href="/wiki/Wolin" title="Wolin">Wollin</a>, off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a>. His date of birth, like his mother\'s name, is unknown. Contemporary works such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Thietmar_of_Merseburg#Thietmar&#39;s_Chronicle" title="Thietmar of Merseburg">Chronicon</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Encomium_Emmae" class="mw-redirect" title="Encomium Emmae">Encomium Emmae</a></i>, do not mention this. Even so, in a <i><a href="/wiki/Kn%C3%BAtsdr%C3%A1pa_(%C3%93ttarr_svarti)" title="Kn\xc3\xbatsdr\xc3\xa1pa (\xc3\x93ttarr svarti)">Kn\xc3\xbatsdr\xc3\xa1pa</a></i> by the <a href="/wiki/Skald" title="Skald">skald</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%93ttarr_svarti" title="\xc3\x93ttarr svarti">\xc3\x93ttarr svarti</a>, there is a statement that Cnut was "of no great age" when he first went to war.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It also mentions a battle identifiable with Sweyn Forkbeard\'s invasion of England and attack on the city of <a href="/wiki/Norwich" title="Norwich">Norwich</a>, in 1003/04, after the <a href="/wiki/St._Brice%27s_Day_massacre" title="St. Brice&#39;s Day massacre">St. Brice\'s Day massacre</a> of Danes by the English, in 1002. If Cnut indeed accompanied this expedition, his birthdate may be near 990, or even 980. If not, and if the skald\'s poetic verse references another assault, such as Forkbeard\'s conquest of England in 1013/14, it may even suggest a birth date nearer 1000.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> There is a passage of the Encomiast (as the author of the <i>Encomium Emmae</i> is known) with a reference to the force Cnut led in his English conquest of 1015/16. Here (<a href="/wiki/Cnut_the_Great#Conquest_of_England" title="Cnut the Great">see below</a>) it says all the Vikings were of "mature age" under Cnut "the king".\n</p><p>A description of Cnut appears in the 13th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Kn%C3%BDtlinga_saga" title="Kn\xc3\xbdtlinga saga">Kn\xc3\xbdtlinga saga</a></i>:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Knut was exceptionally tall and strong, and the handsomest of men, all except for his nose, that was thin, high-set, and rather hooked. He had a fair complexion none-the-less, and a fine, thick head of hair. His eyes were better than those of other men, both the handsomer and the keener of their sight.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><i>Knytlinga Saga</i><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Hardly anything is known for sure of Cnut\'s life until the year he was part of a Scandinavian force under his father, King Sweyn, in his invasion of England in summer 1013. It was the climax to a succession of <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> raids spread over a number of decades. Following their landing in the <a href="/wiki/Humber" title="Humber">Humber</a><sup id="cite_ref-Ellis,_&#39;&#39;Celt_&amp;_Saxon&#39;&#39;,_p._182_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis,_&#39;&#39;Celt_&amp;_Saxon&#39;&#39;,_p._182-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> the kingdom fell to the Vikings quickly, and near the end of the year King <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelred_the_Unready" title="\xc3\x86thelred the Unready">\xc3\x86thelred</a> fled to <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>, leaving Sweyn Forkbeard in possession of England. In the winter, Forkbeard was in the process of consolidating his kingship, with Cnut left in charge of the fleet and the base of the army at <a href="/wiki/Gainsborough,_Lincolnshire" title="Gainsborough, Lincolnshire">Gainsborough</a>.\n</p><p>On the death of Sweyn Forkbeard after a few months as king, on <a href="/wiki/Candlemas" title="Candlemas">Candlemas</a> (Sunday 3 February 1014),<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\nHarald succeeded him as King of Denmark, while the Vikings and the people of the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a> immediately elected Cnut as king in England.<sup id="cite_ref-Sawyer,_p._171_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyer,_p._171-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> However, the English nobility took a different view, and the <a href="/wiki/Witenagemot" title="Witenagemot">Witenagemot</a> recalled \xc3\x86thelred from Normandy. The restored king swiftly led an army against Cnut, who fled with his army to Denmark, along the way mutilating the hostages they had taken and abandoning them on the beach at <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Kent" title="Sandwich, Kent">Sandwich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Cnut went to Harald and supposedly made the suggestion they might have a joint kingship, although this found no favour with his brother.<sup id="cite_ref-Sawyer,_p._171_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyer,_p._171-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Harald is thought to have offered Cnut command of his forces for another invasion of England, on the condition he did not continue to press his claim.<sup id="cite_ref-Sawyer,_p._171_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyer,_p._171-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In any case, Cnut succeeded in assembling a large fleet with which to launch another invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_England">Conquest of England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Conquest of England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U_194,_V%C3%A4sby.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/U_194%2C_V%C3%A4sby.JPG/220px-U_194%2C_V%C3%A4sby.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/U_194%2C_V%C3%A4sby.JPG/330px-U_194%2C_V%C3%A4sby.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/U_194%2C_V%C3%A4sby.JPG/440px-U_194%2C_V%C3%A4sby.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U_194,_V%C3%A4sby.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This <a href="/wiki/Runestone" title="Runestone">runestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/England_Runestones#U_194" class="mw-redirect" title="England Runestones">U 194</a>, in memory of a Viking known as Alli, says he won <i>Kn\xc3\xbatr\'s payment in England</i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Among the allies of Denmark was <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_I_the_Brave" title="Boles\xc5\x82aw I the Brave">Boles\xc5\x82aw I the Brave</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">Duke of Poland</a> (later crowned king) and a relative to the Danish royal house. He lent some <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> troops,<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> likely to have been a pledge made to Cnut and Harald when, in the winter, they "went amongst the <a href="/wiki/Wends" title="Wends">Wends</a>" to fetch their mother back to the Danish court. She had been sent away by their father after the death of the Swedish king <a href="/wiki/Eric_the_Victorious" title="Eric the Victorious">Eric the Victorious</a> in 995, and his marriage to <a href="/wiki/Sigrid_the_Haughty" title="Sigrid the Haughty">Sigrid the Haughty</a>, the Swedish <a href="/wiki/Queen_mother" title="Queen mother">queen mother</a>. This wedlock formed a strong alliance between the successor to the throne of Sweden, <a href="/wiki/Olof_Sk%C3%B6tkonung" title="Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung">Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung</a>, and the rulers of Denmark, his in-laws.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Swedes were certainly among the allies in the English conquest. Another in-law to the Danish royal house, <a href="/wiki/Eir%C3%ADkr_H%C3%A1konarson" title="Eir\xc3\xadkr H\xc3\xa1konarson">Eir\xc3\xadkr H\xc3\xa1konarson</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Jarls_of_Lade" class="mw-redirect" title="Jarls of Lade">Trondejarl</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jarls_of_Lade" class="mw-redirect" title="Jarls of Lade">Earl of Lade</a>) and the co-ruler of Norway, with his brother <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Haakonsson" title="Sweyn Haakonsson">Sweyn Haakonsson</a>\xe2\x80\x94Norway having been under Danish sovereignty since the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Svolder" title="Battle of Svolder">Battle of Svolder</a>, in 999. Eir\xc3\xadkr\'s participation in the invasion left his son Hakon to rule Norway, with Sweyn.\n</p><p>In the summer of 1015, Cnut\'s fleet set sail for England with a Danish army of perhaps 10,000 in 200 longships.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Cnut was at the head of an array of <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> from all over <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>. The invasion force was to engage in often close and grisly warfare with the English for the next fourteen months. Practically all of the battles were fought against the eldest son of \xc3\x86thelred, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Ironside" title="Edmund Ironside">Edmund Ironside</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landing_in_Wessex">Landing in Wessex</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Landing in Wessex">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_Chronicle" title="Peterborough Chronicle">Peterborough Chronicle</a> manuscript, one of the major witnesses of the <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i>, early in September 1015 "[Cnut] came into <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Kent" title="Sandwich, Kent">Sandwich</a>, and straightway sailed around <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>, until he came to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/River_Frome,_Dorset" title="River Frome, Dorset">Frome</a>, and harried in <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wiltshire" title="Wiltshire">Wiltshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> beginning a campaign of an intensity not seen since the days of <a href="/wiki/Alfred_the_Great" title="Alfred the Great">Alfred the Great</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A passage from Emma\'s Encomium provides a picture of Cnut\'s fleet:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>[T]here were there so many kinds of shields, that you could have believed that troops of all nations were present. ... Gold shone on the prows, silver also flashed on the variously shaped ships. ... For who could look upon the lions of the foe, terrible with the brightness of gold, who upon the men of metal, menacing with golden face, ... who upon the bulls on the ships threatening death, their horns shining with gold, without feeling any fear for the king of such a force? Furthermore, in this great expedition there was present no slave, no man freed from slavery, no low-born man, no man weakened by age; for all were noble, all strong with the might of mature age, all sufficiently fit for any type of fighting, all of such great fleetness, that they scorned the speed of horsemen.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><i>Encomium Emmae Reginae</i><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>, long ruled by the dynasty of Alfred and \xc3\x86thelred, submitted to Cnut late in 1015, as it had to his father two years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> At this point <a href="/wiki/Eadric_Streona" title="Eadric Streona">Eadric Streona</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ealdorman_of_Mercia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ealdorman of Mercia">Ealdorman of Mercia</a>, deserted \xc3\x86thelred together with 40 ships and their crews and joined forces with Cnut.<sup id="cite_ref-G._Jones,_Vikings,_p._370_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G._Jones,_Vikings,_p._370-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Another defector was <a href="/wiki/Thorkell_the_Tall" title="Thorkell the Tall">Thorkell the Tall</a>, a Jomsviking chief who had fought against the Viking invasion of <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Forkbeard" title="Sweyn Forkbeard">Sweyn Forkbeard</a>, with a pledge of allegiance to the English in 1012<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94some explanation for this shift of allegiance may be found in a stanza of the <i><a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3msv%C3%ADkinga_saga" title="J\xc3\xb3msv\xc3\xadkinga saga">J\xc3\xb3msv\xc3\xadkinga saga</a></i> that mentions two attacks against Jomsborg\'s mercenaries while they were in England, with a man known as Henninge, a brother of Thorkell, among their casualties.<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._57_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._57-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> If the <i><a href="/wiki/Flateyjarb%C3%B3k" title="Flateyjarb\xc3\xb3k">Flateyjarb\xc3\xb3k</a></i> is correct that this man was Cnut\'s childhood mentor, it explains his acceptance of his allegiance\xe2\x80\x94with <a href="/wiki/Jomvikings" class="mw-redirect" title="Jomvikings">Jomvikings</a> ultimately in the service of <a href="/wiki/Jomsborg" title="Jomsborg">Jomsborg</a>. The 40 ships Eadric came with, often thought to be of the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a><sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._57_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._57-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> were probably Thorkell\'s.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advance_into_the_North">Advance into the North</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Advance into the North">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Early in 1016, the Vikings crossed the <a href="/wiki/Thames" class="mw-redirect" title="Thames">Thames</a> and harried <a href="/wiki/Warwickshire" title="Warwickshire">Warwickshire</a>, while Edmund Ironside\'s attempts at opposition seem to have come to nothing\xe2\x80\x94the chronicler says the English army disbanded because the king and the citizenry of London were not present.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The mid-winter assault by Cnut devastated its way northwards across eastern <a href="/wiki/Mercia" title="Mercia">Mercia</a>. Another summons of the army brought the Englishmen together, and they were met this time by the king, although "it came to nothing as so often before", and \xc3\x86thelred returned to London with fears of betrayal.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._27-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Edmund then went north to join <a href="/wiki/Uhtred,_Earl_of_Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Uhtred, Earl of Northumbria">Uhtred</a> the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Northumbria" title="Earl of Northumbria">Earl of Northumbria</a> and together they harried <a href="/wiki/Staffordshire" title="Staffordshire">Staffordshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shropshire" title="Shropshire">Shropshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a> in western Mercia,<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> possibly targeting the estates of Eadric Streona. Cnut\'s occupation of <a href="/wiki/Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Northumbria">Northumbria</a> meant Uhtred returned home to submit himself to Cnut,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> who seems to have sent a Northumbrian rival, <a href="/wiki/Thurbrand_the_Hold" title="Thurbrand the Hold">Thurbrand the Hold</a>, to massacre Uhtred and his retinue. <a href="/wiki/Eir%C3%ADkr_H%C3%A1konarson" title="Eir\xc3\xadkr H\xc3\xa1konarson">Eir\xc3\xadkr H\xc3\xa1konarson</a>, most likely with another force of Scandinavians, came to support Cnut at this point,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and the veteran Norwegian jarl was put in charge of Northumbria.\n</p><p>Prince Edmund remained in London, still unsubdued behind <a href="/wiki/London_Wall" title="London Wall">its walls</a>, and was elected king after the death of \xc3\x86thelred on 23 April 1016.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Siege_of_London">Siege of London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Siege of London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg/300px-EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg" width="300" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg/450px-EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg/600px-EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1271" data-file-height="636" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EdmundIronside_Canutethe_Dane1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Medieval illumination depicting Kings <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Ironside" title="Edmund Ironside">Edmund Ironside</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Cnut" class="mw-redirect" title="Cnut">Cnut</a> (right), from the <i>Chronica Majora</i> written and illustrated by <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Paris" title="Matthew Paris">Matthew Paris</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Cnut returned southward and the Danish army evidently divided, some dealing with Edmund, who had broken out of London before Cnut\'s encirclement of the city was complete and gone to gather an army in <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>, the traditional heartland of the English monarchy\xe2\x80\x94some besieging London\xe2\x80\x94with the construction of dikes on the northern and southern flanks and a channel dug across the banks of the Thames to the south of the city for the longships to cut off communications up-river.\n</p><p>There was a battle fought at <a href="/wiki/Penselwood" title="Penselwood">Penselwood</a> in <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a>\xe2\x80\x94with a hill in <a href="/wiki/Selwood_Forest" title="Selwood Forest">Selwood Forest</a> as the likely location<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94and a subsequent battle at <a href="/wiki/Sherston,_Wiltshire" title="Sherston, Wiltshire">Sherston</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Wiltshire" title="Wiltshire">Wiltshire</a>, which was fought over two days but left neither side victorious.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Edmund was able to temporarily relieve London, driving the enemy away and defeating them after crossing the Thames at <a href="/wiki/Brentford" title="Brentford">Brentford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Suffering heavy losses, he withdrew to Wessex to gather fresh troops, and the Danes again brought London under siege, but after another unsuccessful assault they withdrew into <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> under attack by the English, with a battle fought at <a href="/wiki/Otford" title="Otford">Otford</a>. At this point Eadric Streona went over to King Edmund,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and Cnut set sail northwards across the Thames estuary to <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, and went from the landing of the ships up the <a href="/wiki/River_Orwell" title="River Orwell">River Orwell</a> to ravage Mercia.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="London_captured_by_treaty">London captured by treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: London captured by treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 18 October 1016, the Danes were engaged by Edmund\'s army as they retired towards their ships, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Assandun" title="Battle of Assandun">Battle of Assandun</a>, fought at either <a href="/wiki/Ashingdon" title="Ashingdon">Ashingdon</a>, in south-east, or <a href="/wiki/Ashdon" title="Ashdon">Ashdon</a>, in north-west <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>. In the ensuing struggle, Eadric Streona, whose return to the English side had perhaps only been a ruse, withdrew his forces from the fray, bringing about a decisive English defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Edmund fled westwards, and Cnut pursued him into <a href="/wiki/Gloucestershire" title="Gloucestershire">Gloucestershire</a>, with another battle probably fought near the <a href="/wiki/Forest_of_Dean" title="Forest of Dean">Forest of Dean</a>, for Edmund had an alliance with some of the Welsh.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p.28-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On an island near <a href="/wiki/Deerhurst" title="Deerhurst">Deerhurst</a>, Cnut and Edmund, who had been wounded,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="Please clarify the following statement or statements with a good explanation from a reliable source. (August 2018)">how?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> met to negotiate terms of peace. It was agreed that all of England north of the Thames was to be the domain of the Danish prince, while all to the south was kept by the English king, along with London. Accession to the reign of the entire realm was set to pass to Cnut upon Edmund\'s death. Edmund died on 30 November, within weeks of the arrangement. Some sources claim Edmund was murdered, although the circumstances of his death are unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  The West Saxons now accepted Cnut as king of all of England,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and he was crowned by <a href="/wiki/Lyfing_(Archbishop_of_Canterbury)" title="Lyfing (Archbishop of Canterbury)">Lyfing, Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, in London in 1017.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="King_of_England">King of England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: King of England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Cnut ruled <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> for nearly two decades. The protection he lent against Viking raiders\xe2\x80\x94many of them under his command\xe2\x80\x94restored the prosperity that had been increasingly impaired since the resumption of Viking attacks in the <a href="/wiki/10th_century_in_England" title="10th century in England">980s</a>. In turn the English helped him to establish control over the majority of <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>, too.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consolidation_and_Danegeld">Consolidation and Danegeld</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Consolidation and Danegeld">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As Danish King of England, Cnut was quick to eliminate any prospective challenge from the survivors of the mighty Wessex dynasty. The first year of his reign was marked by the executions of a number of English noblemen whom he considered suspect. <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelred_the_Unready" title="\xc3\x86thelred the Unready">\xc3\x86thelred</a>\'s son <a href="/wiki/Eadwig_%C3%86theling" title="Eadwig \xc3\x86theling">Eadwig \xc3\x86theling</a> fled from England but was killed on Cnut\'s orders.<sup id="cite_ref-Anglo-Saxon_Chronicles,_p._154_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anglo-Saxon_Chronicles,_p._154-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Edmund Ironside\'s sons likewise fled abroad. \xc3\x86thelred\'s sons by <a href="/wiki/Emma_of_Normandy" title="Emma of Normandy">Emma of Normandy</a> went under the protection of their relatives in the <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> duchy.\n</p><p>In July 1017, Cnut wed queen Emma, the widow of \xc3\x86thelred and daughter of <a href="/wiki/Richard_I,_Duke_of_Normandy" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard I, Duke of Normandy">Richard I, Duke of Normandy</a>. Later he was to proclaim <a href="/wiki/Harthacnut" title="Harthacnut">Harthacnut</a>, his son by Emma, to be his heir; while <a href="/wiki/Svein_Knutsson" title="Svein Knutsson">Svein Knutsson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Harefoot" title="Harold Harefoot">Harold Harefoot</a>, his two sons from his marriage to <a href="/wiki/%C3%86lfgifu_of_Northampton" title="\xc3\x86lfgifu of Northampton">\xc3\x86lfgifu of Northampton</a>, his <a href="/wiki/History_of_marriage_in_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="History of marriage in Great Britain and Ireland">handfast</a> wife, were kept on the sidelines in the running to the throne.\n</p><p>In 1018, having collected a <a href="/wiki/Danegeld" title="Danegeld">Danegeld</a> amounting to the colossal sum of \xc2\xa372,000 levied nationwide, with an additional \xc2\xa310,500 extracted from London, Cnut paid off his army and sent most of them home. He retained 40 ships and their crews as a standing force in England. An annual tax called <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_medieval_England" title="Taxation in medieval England">heregeld</a> (army payment) was collected through the same system \xc3\x86thelred had instituted in 1012 to reward Scandinavians in his service.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_pp._51\xe2\x80\x9352,_163_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_pp._51\xe2\x80\x9352,_163-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cnut built on the existing English trend for multiple <a href="/wiki/Shire" title="Shire">shires</a> to be grouped together under a single <a href="/wiki/Ealdorman" title="Ealdorman">ealdorman</a>, thusly dividing the country into four large administrative units whose geographical extent was based on the largest and most durable of the separate kingdoms that had preceded the unification of England. The officials responsible for these provinces were designated <a href="/wiki/Earl" title="Earl">earls</a>, a title of Scandinavian origin already in localised use in England, which now everywhere replaced that of ealdorman. Wessex was initially kept under Cnut\'s personal control, while Northumbria went to <a href="/wiki/Erik_of_Hlathir" class="mw-redirect" title="Erik of Hlathir">Erik of Hlathir</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Anglia" title="East Anglia">East Anglia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Thorkell_the_Tall" title="Thorkell the Tall">Thorkell the Tall</a>, and Mercia remained in the hands of <a href="/wiki/Eadric_Streona" title="Eadric Streona">Eadric Streona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._83_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._83-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This initial distribution of power was short-lived. The chronically treacherous Eadric was executed within a year of Cnut\'s accession.<sup id="cite_ref-Anglo-Saxon_Chronicles,_p._154_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anglo-Saxon_Chronicles,_p._154-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Mercia passed to one of the leading families of the region, probably first to <a href="/wiki/Leofwine,_Earl_of_Mercia" class="mw-redirect" title="Leofwine, Earl of Mercia">Leofwine</a>, ealdorman of the <a href="/wiki/Hwicce" title="Hwicce">Hwicce</a> under \xc3\x86thelred, but certainly soon to his son <a href="/wiki/Leofric,_Earl_of_Mercia" title="Leofric, Earl of Mercia">Leofric</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 1021 Thorkel also fell from favour and was outlawed. Following the death of Erik in the 1020s, he was succeeded as Earl of Northumbria by <a href="/wiki/Siward_of_Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Siward of Northumbria">Siward</a>, whose grandmother,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Estrid (married to \xc3\x9alfr Thorgilsson), was Cnut\'s sister. <a href="/wiki/Bernicia" title="Bernicia">Bernicia</a>, the northern part of Northumbria, was theoretically part of Erik and Siward\'s earldom, but throughout Cnut\'s reign it effectively remained under the control of the English dynasty based at <a href="/wiki/Bamburgh" title="Bamburgh">Bamburgh</a>, which had dominated the area at least since the early 10th century. They served as junior Earls of Bernicia under the titular authority of the Earl of Northumbria. By the 1030s Cnut\'s direct administration of Wessex had come to an end, with the establishment of an earldom under <a href="/wiki/Godwin,_Earl_of_Wessex" title="Godwin, Earl of Wessex">Godwin</a>, an Englishman from a powerful <a href="/wiki/Sussex" title="Sussex">Sussex</a> family. In general, after initial reliance on his Scandinavian followers in the first years of his reign, Cnut allowed those Anglo-Saxon families of the existing English nobility who had earned his trust to assume rulership of his Earldoms.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Affairs_to_the_East">Affairs to the East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Affairs to the East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg/220px-Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg/330px-Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg/440px-Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="534" data-file-height="263" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_1016_1035_a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coins of Cnut the Great, <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nesjar" title="Battle of Nesjar">Battle of Nesjar</a>, in 1016, <a href="/wiki/Olaf_II_of_Norway" title="Olaf II of Norway">Olaf Haraldsson</a> won the kingdom of Norway from the Danes. It was at some time after Eirkr left for England, and on the death of Svein while retreating to Sweden, maybe intent on returning to Norway with reinforcements, that Erikr\'s son Hakon went to join his father and support Cnut in England, too.\n</p><p>Cnut\'s brother Harald may have been at Cnut\'s coronation, in 1016, returning to Denmark as its king, with part of the fleet, at some point thereafter. It is only certain, though, that there was an entry of his name, alongside Cnut\'s, in confraternity with <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_Cathedral" title="Canterbury Cathedral">Christ Church, Canterbury</a>, in 1018.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._89_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._89-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> This is not conclusive, though, for the entry may have been made in Harald\'s absence, perhaps by the hand of Cnut himself, which means that, while it is usually thought that Harald died in 1018, it is unsure whether he was still alive at this point.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._89_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._89-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Entry of his brother\'s name in the Canterbury <a href="/wiki/Codex" title="Codex">codex</a> may have been Cnut\'s attempt to make his vengeance for Harald\'s murder good with the Church. This may have been just a gesture for a soul to be under the protection of God. There is evidence Cnut was in battle with <i>pirates</i> in 1018, with his destruction of the crews of thirty ships,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> although it is unknown if this was off the English or Danish shores. He himself mentions troubles in his 1019 letter (to England, from Denmark), written as the King of England and Denmark. These events can be seen, with plausibility, to be in connection with the death of Harald. Cnut says he dealt with dissenters to ensure Denmark was free to assist England:<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>King Cnut greets in friendship his archbishop and his diocesan bishops and Earl Thurkil and all his earls ... ecclesiastic and lay, in England ... I inform you that I will be a gracious lord and a faithfull observer of God\'s rights and just secular law. (He exhorts his ealdormen to assist the bishops in the maintenance of) God\'s rights ... and the benefit of the people.\n</p><p>If anyone, ecclesiastic or layman, Dane or Englishman, is so presumptuous as to defy God\'s law and my royal authority or the secular laws, and he will not make amends and desist according to the direction of my bishops, I then pray, and also command, Earl Thurkil, if he can, to cause the evil-doer to do right. And if he cannot, then it is my will that with the power of us both he shall destroy him in the land or drive him out of the land, whether he be of high or low rank. And it is my will that all the nation, ecclesiastical and lay, shall steadfastly observe Edgar\'s laws, which all men have chosen and sworn at Oxford.\n</p><p>\nSince I did not spare my money, as long as hostility was threatening you, I with God\'s help have put an end to it. Then I was informed that greater danger was approaching us than we liked at all; and then I went myself with the men who accompanied me to Denmark, from where the greatest injury had come to us, and with God\'s help I have made it so that never henceforth shall hostility reach you from there as long as you support me rightly and my life lasts. Now I thank Almighty God for his help and his mercy, that I have settled the great dangers which were approaching us that we need fear no danger to us from there; but we may rekon on full help and deliverance, if we need it.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><i>Cnut\'s letter of 1019</i><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statesmanship">Statesmanship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Statesmanship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg/220px-Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg/330px-Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg/440px-Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="536" data-file-height="268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_1016_1035_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coins of Cnut the Great, <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cnut was generally remembered as a wise and successful king of England, although this view may in part be attributable to his good treatment of the Church, keeper of the historic record. Accordingly, we hear of him, even today, as a religious man (<a href="/wiki/Cnut_the_Great#Ruler_of_the_waves" title="Cnut the Great">see below</a>), despite the fact that he was in an arguably <a href="/wiki/Sin" title="Sin">sinful</a> relationship, with two wives, and the harsh treatment he dealt his fellow Christian opponents.\n</p><p>Under his reign, Cnut brought together the English and Danish kingdoms, and the Scandinavic and Saxon peoples saw a period of dominance across <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>, as well as within the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> His campaigns abroad meant the tables of Viking supremacy were stacked in favour of the English, turning the prows of the longships towards Scandinavia. He reinstated the Laws of <a href="/wiki/Edgar_the_Peaceful" title="Edgar the Peaceful">King Edgar</a> to allow for the constitution of a <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and for the activity of Scandinavians at large. He also reinstituted the extant laws with a series of proclamations to assuage common grievances brought to his attention, including: <i>On <a href="/wiki/Inheritance" title="Inheritance">Inheritance</a> in case of <a href="/wiki/Intestacy" title="Intestacy">Intestacy</a></i>, and <i>On <a href="/wiki/Heriot" title="Heriot">Heriots</a> and Reliefs</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> He also strengthened the currency, initiating a series of coins of equal weight to those being used in Denmark and other parts of Scandinavia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="King_of_Denmark">King of Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: King of Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Harald II died in 1018, and Cnut went to Denmark to affirm his succession to the Danish crown as Cnut II, stating his intention to avert attacks against England in a letter in 1019 (<a href="/wiki/Cnut_the_Great#Affairs_to_the_East" title="Cnut the Great">see above</a>). It seems there were Danes in opposition to him, and an attack he carried out on the <a href="/wiki/Wends" title="Wends">Wends</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a> may have had something to do with this. In this expedition, at least one of Cnut\'s Englishmen, Godwin, apparently won the king\'s trust after a night-time raid he personally led against a Wendish encampment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>His hold on the Danish throne presumably stable, Cnut was back in England in 1020. He appointed <a href="/wiki/Ulf_Jarl" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulf Jarl">Ulf Jarl</a>, the husband of his sister <a href="/wiki/Estrid_Svendsdatter" title="Estrid Svendsdatter">Estrid Svendsdatter</a>, as regent of Denmark, further entrusting him with his young son by <a href="/wiki/Emma_of_Normandy" title="Emma of Normandy">Queen Emma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harthacnut" title="Harthacnut">Harthacnut</a>, whom he had made the <a href="/wiki/Crown_prince" title="Crown prince">crown prince</a> of his kingdom. The banishment of Thorkell the Tall in 1021 may be seen in relation to the attack on the Wends. With the death of <a href="/wiki/Olof_Sk%C3%B6tkonung" title="Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung">Olof Sk\xc3\xb6tkonung</a> in 1022, and the succession to the Swedish throne of his son <a href="/wiki/Anund_Jacob_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Anund Jacob of Sweden">Anund Jacob</a> bringing Sweden into alliance with Norway, there was cause for a demonstration of Danish strength in the Baltic. <a href="/wiki/Jomsborg" title="Jomsborg">Jomsborg</a>, the legendary stronghold of the Jomsvikings (thought to be on an island off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a>), was probably the target of Cnut\'s expedition.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Successful, after this clear display of Cnut\'s intentions to dominate Scandinavian affairs, it seems that Thorkell reconciled with Cnut in 1023.\n</p><p>When, in spite of this, the Norwegian king <a href="/wiki/Olaf_II_of_Norway" title="Olaf II of Norway">Olaf Haraldsson</a> and Anund Jakob took advantage of Cnut\'s commitment to England and began to launch attacks against Denmark, Ulf gave the Danish freemen cause to accept Harthacnut, still a child, as king. This was a ruse on Ulf\'s part since his role as caretaker of Harthacnut gave him the reign of the kingdom. Upon news of these events, Cnut set sail for Denmark to restore himself and to deal with Ulf, who then got back in line. In a battle known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Helge%C3%A5" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the Helge\xc3\xa5">Battle of the Helge\xc3\xa5</a>, Cnut and his men fought the Norwegians and Swedes at the mouth of the river Helgea, probably in 1026, and the apparent victory left Cnut as the dominant leader in Scandinavia. Ulf the usurper\'s realignment and participation in the battle did not, in the end, earn him Cnut\'s forgiveness.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Some sources state that the brothers-in-law were playing <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> at a banquet in <a href="/wiki/Roskilde" title="Roskilde">Roskilde</a> when an argument arose between them, and the next day, <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> 1026, one of Cnut\'s <a href="/wiki/Housecarl" title="Housecarl">housecarls</a> killed the jarl with his blessing, in Trinity Church, the predecessor to <a href="/wiki/Roskilde_Cathedral" title="Roskilde Cathedral">Roskilde Cathedral</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Journey_to_Rome">Journey to Rome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Journey to Rome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg/220px-Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg/330px-Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg/440px-Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="559" data-file-height="288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_1016_1035_c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coins of Cnut the Great, <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>His enemies in Scandinavia subdued, and apparently at his leisure, Cnut was able to accept an invitation to witness the accession of the Holy Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Conrad_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Conrad II, Holy Roman Emperor">Conrad II</a>. He left his affairs in the north and went from Denmark to the coronation at Easter 1027 in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>\xe2\x80\x94a pilgrimage to the heart of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a> being of considerable prestige for rulers of Europe in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. On the return journey he wrote his letter of 1027, like his letter of 1019, informing his subjects in England of his intentions from abroad<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and proclaiming himself "king of all England and Denmark and the Norwegians and of some of the Swedes".<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Consistent with his role as a Christian king, Cnut says he went to <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> to repent for his sins, to pray for redemption and the security of his subjects, and to negotiate with the Pope for a reduction in the costs of the <a href="/wiki/Pallium" title="Pallium">pallium</a> for English archbishops,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and for a resolution to the competition between the archdioceses of <a href="/wiki/Canterbury" title="Canterbury">Canterbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Bremen" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Bremen">Hamburg-Bremen</a> for superiority over the Danish dioceses. He also sought to improve the conditions for pilgrims, as well as merchants, on the road to Rome. In his own words:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>...&#160;I spoke with the Emperor himself and the Lord Pope and the princes there about the needs of all people of my entire realm, both English and Danes, that a juster law and securer peace might be granted to them on the road to Rome and that they should not be straitened by so many barriers along the road, and harassed by unjust tolls; and the Emperor agreed and likewise King Robert who governs most of these same toll gates. And all the magnates confirmed by edict that my people, both merchants, and the others who travel to make their devotions, might go to Rome and return without being afflicted by barriers and toll collectors, in firm peace and secure in a just law.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><i>Cnut\'s letter of 1027</i><sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>"Robert" in Cnut\'s text is probably a clerical error for <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_III_of_Burgundy" title="Rudolph III of Burgundy">Rudolph</a>, the last ruler of an independent <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Burgundy" title="Kingdom of Burgundy">Kingdom of Burgundy</a>. Hence, the solemn word of the Pope, the Emperor and Rudolph was given with the witness of four archbishops, twenty bishops, and "innumerable multitudes of dukes and nobles",<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> suggesting it was before the ceremonies were completed.<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Cnut without doubt threw himself into his role with zest.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_&#39;&#39;Cnut&#39;&#39;,_p._125._52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_&#39;&#39;Cnut&#39;&#39;,_p._125.-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> His image as a just Christian king, statesman and diplomat and crusader against unjustness, seems rooted in reality, as well as one he sought to project.\n</p><p>A good illustration of his status within Europe is the fact that Cnut and the <a href="/wiki/Kings_of_Burgundy" class="mw-redirect" title="Kings of Burgundy">King of Burgundy</a> went alongside the emperor in the imperial procession<sup id="cite_ref-Forte,_p._198_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forte,_p._198-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and stood shoulder-to-shoulder with him on the same pedestal.<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._189_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._189-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Cnut and the emperor, in accord with various sources,<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._189_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._189-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> took to one another\'s company like brothers, for they were of a similar age. Conrad gave Cnut lands in the <a href="/wiki/Marches" class="mw-redirect" title="Marches">Mark</a> of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Schleswig" title="Duchy of Schleswig">Schleswig</a>\xe2\x80\x94the land-bridge between the Scandinavian kingdoms and the continent\xe2\x80\x94as a token of their treaty of friendship.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Centuries of conflict in this area between the Danes and the Germans led to construction of the <a href="/wiki/Danevirke" title="Danevirke">Danevirke</a>, from Schleswig, on the <a href="/wiki/Schlei" title="Schlei">Schlei</a>, an inlet of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>.\n</p><p>Cnut\'s visit to Rome was a triumph. In the verse of <i><a href="/wiki/Kn%C3%BAtsdr%C3%A1pa" title="Kn\xc3\xbatsdr\xc3\xa1pa">Kn\xc3\xbatsdr\xc3\xa1pa</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Sigvatr_%C3%9E%C3%B3r%C3%B0arson" title="Sigvatr \xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3r\xc3\xb0arson">Sigvatr \xc3\x9e\xc3\xb3r\xc3\xb0arson</a> praises Cnut, his king, as being "dear to the Emperor, close to Peter".<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._191_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._191-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In the days of Christendom, a king seen to be in favour with God could expect to be ruler over a happy kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._191_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._191-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He was surely in a stronger position, not only with the Church and the people, but also in the alliance with his southern rivals he was able to conclude his conflicts with his rivals in the north. His letter not only tells his countrymen of his achievements in Rome, but also of his ambitions within the Scandinavian world at his arrival home:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>...&#160;I, as I wish to be made known to you, returning by the same route that I took out, am going to Denmark to arrange peace and a firm treaty, in the counsel of all the Danes, with those races and people who would have deprived us of life and rule if they could, but they could not, God destroying their strength. May he preserve us by his bounteous compassion in rule and honour and henceforth scatter and bring to nothing the power and might of all our enemies! And finally, when peace has been arranged with our surrounding peoples and all our kingdom here in the east has been properly ordered and pacified, so that we have no war to fear on any side or the hostility of individuals, I intend to come to England as early this summer as I can to attend to the equipping of a fleet.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><i>Cnut\'s letter of 1027</i><sup id="cite_ref-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trow,_Cnut,_p._193-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Cnut was to return to Denmark from Rome, arrange for its security,<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and afterwards sail to England.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="King_of_Norway_and_Sweden">King of Norway and Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: King of Norway and Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_lands.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Cnut_lands.svg/220px-Cnut_lands.svg.png" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Cnut_lands.svg/330px-Cnut_lands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Cnut_lands.svg/440px-Cnut_lands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="642" data-file-height="511" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cnut_lands.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The North Sea Empire of Cnut the Great, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1030. (Note that the Norwegian lands of <a href="/wiki/Jemtland" class="mw-redirect" title="Jemtland">Jemtland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herjedalen" class="mw-redirect" title="Herjedalen">Herjedalen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idre" title="Idre">Idre</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A4rna" title="S\xc3\xa4rna">S\xc3\xa6rna</a> are not included in this map.)</div></div></div>\n<p>In his 1027 letter, Cnut refers to himself as king of "the Norwegians, and of some of the Swedes" \xe2\x80\x94 his victory over Swedes suggests Helgea to be the river in <a href="/wiki/Uppland" title="Uppland">Uppland</a> and not the one in eastern <a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 while the king of Sweden appears to have been made a renegade.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_pp._95\xe2\x80\x938_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_pp._95\xe2\x80\x938-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Cnut also stated his intention of proceeding to Denmark to secure peace between the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>, which fits the account of <a href="/wiki/John_of_Worcester" title="John of Worcester">John of Worcester</a> that in 1027 Cnut heard some Norwegians were discontented and sent them sums of gold and silver to gain their support in his claim on the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1028, after his return from Rome through Denmark, Cnut set off from England to Norway, and the city of <a href="/wiki/Trondheim" title="Trondheim">Trondheim</a>, with a fleet of fifty ships.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p._97-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Olaf_II_of_Norway" title="Olaf II of Norway">Olaf Haraldsson</a> stood down, unable to put up any fight, as his nobles were against him for his tendency to flay their wives for sorcery.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Cnut was crowned king, now of England, Denmark and Norway as well as part of Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawson,_Cnut,_p_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawson,_Cnut,_p-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He entrusted the Earldom of <a href="/wiki/Lade,_Trondheim" title="Lade, Trondheim">Lade</a> to the former line of earls, in <a href="/wiki/Haakon_Ericsson" title="Haakon Ericsson">H\xc3\xa5kon Eiriksson</a>, with Eir\xc3\xadkr H\xc3\xa1konarson probably dead by this time.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Hakon was possibly the Earl of Northumbria after Erik as well.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hakon, a member of a family with a long tradition of hostility towards the independent Norwegian kings, and a relative of Cnut\'s, was already in lordship over the Isles with the earldom of <a href="/wiki/Worcester" title="Worcester">Worcester</a>, possibly from 1016 to 1017. The sea-lanes through the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a> led to <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, and were central to Cnut\'s ambitions for dominance of Scandinavia and the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>. Hakon was meant to be Cnut\'s lieutenant in this strategic chain, and the final component was his installation as the king\'s deputy in Norway, after the expulsion of Olaf Haraldsson in 1028. Unfortunately, he was drowned in a shipwreck in the <a href="/wiki/Pentland_Firth" title="Pentland Firth">Pentland Firth</a> (between the <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkneys</a> and the mainland coast) either late 1029 or early 1030.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Upon the death of Hakon, Olaf Haraldsson returned to Norway, with Swedes in his army. He died at the hands of his own people, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stiklestad" title="Battle of Stiklestad">Battle of Stiklestad</a> in 1030. Cnut\'s subsequent attempt to rule Norway without the key support of the <a href="/wiki/Jarls_of_Lade" class="mw-redirect" title="Jarls of Lade">Trondejarls</a>, through <a href="/wiki/%C3%86lfgifu_of_Northampton" title="\xc3\x86lfgifu of Northampton">\xc3\x86lfgifu of Northampton</a>, and his eldest son by her, <a href="/wiki/Svein_Knutsson" title="Svein Knutsson">Sweyn Knutsson</a>, was not a success. The period is known as <i>Aelfgifu\'s Time</i> in Norway, with heavy taxation, a rebellion, and the restoration of the former Norwegian dynasty under Saint Olaf\'s illegitimate son <a href="/wiki/Magnus_I_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnus I of Norway">Magnus the Good</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_in_the_western_sea-ways">Influence in the western sea-ways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cnut_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Influence in the western sea-ways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1014, while Cnut was preparing his re-invasion of England, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Clontarf" title="Battle of Clontarf">Battle of Clontarf</a> pitted an array of armies laid out on the fields before the walls of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. M\xc3\xa1el M\xc3\xb3rda, king of <a href="/wiki/Leinster" title="Leinster">Leinster</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sigtrygg_Silkbeard" title="Sigtrygg Silkbeard">Sigtrygg Silkbeard</a>, ruler of the Norse-Gaelic kingdom of Dublin, had sent out emissaries to all the Viking kingdoms to request assistance in their rebellion against <a href="/wiki/Brian_B%C3%B3ruma" class="mw-redirect" title="Brian B\xc3\xb3ruma">Brian B\xc3\xb3ruma</a>, the <a href="/wiki/High_King_of_Ireland" title="High King of Ireland">High King of Ireland</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sigurd_the_Stout" title="Sigurd the Stout">Sigurd the Stout</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Orkney" title="Earl of Orkney">Earl of Orkney</a>, was offered command of all the Norse forces, while the High King had sought assistance from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Albanaich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Albanaich (page does not exist)">Albanaich</a>, who were led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Domhnall_Mac_Eiminn_Mac_Cainnich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Domhnall Mac Eiminn Mac Cainnich (page does not exist)">Domhnall Mac Eiminn Mac Cainnich</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mormaer_of_Ce_(Marr_%26_Buchan)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mormaer of Ce (Marr &amp; Buchan) (page does not exist)">Mormaer of Ce (Marr &amp; Buchan)</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Leinster-Norse alliance was defeated, and both commanders, Sigurd and M\xc3\xa1el M\xc3\xb3rda, were killed. Brian, his son, his grandson, and the Mormaer Domhnall were slain as well. Sigtrygg\'s alliance was broken, although he was left alive, and the high-kingship of Ireland went back to the <a href="/wiki/U%C3%AD_N%C3%A9ill" title="U\xc3\xad N\xc3\xa9ill">U\xc3\xad N\xc3\xa9ill</a>, again under <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1el_Sechnaill_mac_Domnaill" title="M\xc3\xa1el Sechnaill mac Domnaill">M\xc3\xa1el Sechnaill mac Domnaill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ellis,_&#39;&#39;Celt_&amp;_Saxon&#39;&#39;,_p._182_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis,_&#39;&#39;Celt_&amp;_Saxon&#39;&#39;,_p._182-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was a brief period of freedom in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> zone for the Vikings of Dublin, with a political vacuum felt throughout the entire Western Maritime Zone of the North Atlantic Archipelago.
